<dd class="glossary">Any chemical species that readily donates a&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#proton"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; proton">proton</span></a>.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="br&oslash;nsted&ndash;lowry_acid&ndash;base_reaction" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Br&oslash;nsted&ndash;Lowry acid&ndash;base theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Br%C3%B8nsted%E2%80%93Lowry_acid%E2%80%93base_theory">Br&oslash;nsted&ndash;Lowry acid&ndash;base reaction</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="br&oslash;nsted&ndash;lowry_base" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Br&oslash;nsted&ndash;Lowry acid&ndash;base theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Br%C3%B8nsted%E2%80%93Lowry_acid%E2%80%93base_theory">Br&oslash;nsted&ndash;Lowry base</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Any chemical species that readily accepts a&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#proton"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; proton">proton</span></a>.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="b&uuml;chner_flask" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="B&uuml;chner flask" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/B%C3%BCchner_flask">B&uuml;chner flask</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="buffered_solution" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Buffered solution" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buffered_solution">buffered solution</a></dfn></dt>
</dl>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><span class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also simply called a&nbsp;<strong>buffer</strong>.</span></p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dd class="glossary">An&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#aqueous_solution"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; aqueous solution">aqueous solution</span></a>&nbsp;consisting of a weak&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#acid"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; acid">acid</span></a>&nbsp;and its&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#conjugate_base"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; conjugate base">conjugate base</span></a>&nbsp;or a weak&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#base"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; base">base</span></a>&nbsp;and its&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#conjugate_acid"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; conjugate acid">conjugate acid</span></a>&nbsp;that resists changes in&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#pH"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; pH">pH</span></a>&nbsp;when strong acids or bases are added.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="bumping" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Bumping (chemistry)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bumping_(chemistry)">bumping</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A phenomenon in which a homogeneous liquid raised to its&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#boiling_point"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; boiling point">boiling point</span></a>&nbsp;becomes&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#superheating"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; superheating">superheated</span></a>&nbsp;and, upon&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#nucleation"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; nucleation">nucleation</span></a>, rapidly boils to the gas phase, resulting in a violent expulsion of the liquid from the container; in extreme cases, the container itself may shatter. Frequent stirring, the use of an appropriate container, and the use of&nbsp;<a title="Boiling chip" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boiling_chip">boiling chips</a>&nbsp;can help prevent bumping.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="bung" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Bung" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bung">bung</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="burette" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Burette" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Burette">burette</a></dfn></dt>
</dl>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><span class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also spelled&nbsp;<strong>buret</strong>.</span></p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dd class="glossary">Glassware used to dispense specific amounts of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#liquid"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; liquid">liquid</span></a>&nbsp;when precision is necessary (e.g. during&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#titration"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; titration">titrations</span></a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#resource_dependent_reaction"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; resource dependent reaction">resource-dependent reactions</span></a>).</dd>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
</dl>
<h2><span id="C" class="mw-headline">C</span></h2>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="calorimeter" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Calorimeter" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Calorimeter">calorimeter</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A device used to measure&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#heat"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; heat">heat</span></a>.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="carbanion" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Carbanion" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carbanion">carbanion</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="carbocation" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Carbocation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carbocation">carbocation</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="catalyst" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Catalyst" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Catalyst">catalyst</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Any element or compound that facilitates an increase in the speed of a&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemical_reaction"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; chemical reaction">chemical reaction</span></a>&nbsp;but which is not consumed or destroyed during the reaction. It is considered both a&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#reactant"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; reactant">reactant</span></a>&nbsp;and a&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#product"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; product">product</span></a>&nbsp;of the reaction.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="cathode" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Cathode" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cathode">cathode</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electrode"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; electrode">electrode</span></a>&nbsp;from which the conventional&nbsp;<a title="Electric current" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electric_current">electric current</a>&nbsp;(the flow of positive charges) exits a&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#polarity"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; polarity">polarized</span></a>&nbsp;electrical circuit. Positively charged&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#cation"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; cation">cations</span></a>&nbsp;always move toward the cathode, though the cathode's polarity can be positive or negative depending on the type of electrical device and how it is being operated. Contrast&nbsp;<em><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#anode"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; anode">anode</span></a></em>.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="cation" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Cation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cation">cation</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A positively charged&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#ion"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; ion">ion</span></a>.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="centrifugation" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Centrifugation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Centrifugation">centrifugation</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A laboratory technique which involves the application of centrifugal force to separate particles from a&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solution"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; solution">solution</span></a>&nbsp;according to their size, shape, and density. Larger and/or denser substances migrate away from the axis of a&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#centrifuge"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; centrifuge">centrifuge</span></a>, while smaller and/or less dense substances migrate towards the axis.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="centrifuge" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Centrifuge" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Centrifuge">centrifuge</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A device used to separate substances based on size, shape, and density by&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#centrifugation"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; centrifugation">centrifugation</span></a>, or the rotation of vessels containing the substances around a centred axis at extremely high velocities.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="cell_potential" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Resting potential" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Resting_potential">cell potential</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The force in a&nbsp;<a title="Galvanic cell" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Galvanic_cell">galvanic cell</a>&nbsp;that pulls electrons through a reducing agent to an oxidizing agent.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="chain_reaction" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Chain reaction" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chain_reaction">chain reaction</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="charge_number" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Charge number" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charge_number">charge number</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A&nbsp;<a title="Quantification (science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantification_(science)">quantized</a>&nbsp;value of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electric_charge"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; electric charge">electric charge</span></a>&nbsp;calculated as the electric charge in&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#coulomb"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; coulomb">coulombs</span></a>&nbsp;divided by the&nbsp;<a title="Elementary charge" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elementary_charge">elementary-charge</a>&nbsp;constant, or&nbsp;<em>z = q/e</em>. Charge numbers for&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#ion"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; ion">ions</span></a>&nbsp;are denoted in superscript (e.g. Na<sup>+</sup>&nbsp;indicates a&nbsp;<a title="Sodium" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sodium">sodium</a>&nbsp;ion with a charge number of positive one).&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#atomic_number"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; atomic number">Atomic numbers</span></a>&nbsp;are charge numbers of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#nucleus"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; nucleus">atomic nuclei</span></a>.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="charles's_law" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Charles's law" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles%27s_law">Charles's law</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">When the pressure on a sample of a dry gas is held constant, the Kelvin temperature is directly proportional to its volume.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="chelating_agent" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Chelating agent" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chelating_agent">chelating agent</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="chelation" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Chelation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chelation">chelation</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A type of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#bond"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; bond">bonding</span></a>&nbsp;involving the formation of two separate&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#coordinate_covalent_bond"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; coordinate covalent bond">coordinate covalent bonds</span></a>&nbsp;between a&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#denticity"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; denticity">polydentate</span></a>&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#ligand"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; ligand">ligand</span></a>&nbsp;and a single central&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#metal"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; metal">metal</span></a>&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#ion"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; ion">ion</span></a>. The ligand is usually an&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#organic_compound"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; organic compound">organic compound</span></a>&nbsp;called a&nbsp;<em>chelant</em>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<em><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chelating_agent"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; chelating agent">chelating agent</span></a></em>.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="chemical_composition" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Chemical composition" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chemical_composition">chemical composition</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The identity and relative number of the&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#element"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; element">elements</span></a>&nbsp;that make up a&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#compound"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; compound">chemical compound</span></a>, which can often be expressed with a&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemical_formula"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; chemical formula">chemical formula</span></a>.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="chemical_decomposition" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Chemical decomposition" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chemical_decomposition">chemical decomposition</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The breakdown of a single particle or entity (such as a&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#molecule"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; molecule">molecule</span></a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#reactive_intermediate"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; reactive intermediate">reactive intermediate</span></a>) into two or more fragments, or a&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemical_reaction"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; chemical reaction">chemical reaction</span></a>&nbsp;in which two or more&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#product"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; product">products</span></a>&nbsp;are formed from a single&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#reactant"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; reactant">reactant</span></a>. Contrast&nbsp;<em><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemical_synthesis"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; chemical synthesis">chemical synthesis</span></a></em>.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="chemical_formula" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Chemical formula" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chemical_formula">chemical formula</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Any of various means of concisely displaying information about the&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemical_composition"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; chemical composition">chemical composition</span></a>&nbsp;of a&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#compound"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; compound">compound</span></a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#molecule"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; molecule">molecule</span></a>&nbsp;using letters, numbers, and/or typographical symbols. Chemical formulas, such as&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#empirical_formula"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; empirical formula">empirical</span></a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#molecular_formula"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; molecular formula">molecular formulas</span></a>, can only indicate the identities and numerical proportions of the atoms in a compound and are therefore more limited in descriptive power than&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemical_nomenclature"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; chemical nomenclature">chemical names</span></a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#structural_formula"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; structural formula">structural formulas</span></a>.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="chemical_law" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Chemical law" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chemical_law">chemical law</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Physical law" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Physical_law">law of nature</a>&nbsp;relevant to&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemistry"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; chemistry">chemistry</span></a>, such as the&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#law_of_conservation_of_mass"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; law of conservation of mass">law of conservation of mass</span></a>.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="chemical_nomenclature" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Chemical nomenclature" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chemical_nomenclature">chemical nomenclature</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="chemical_process" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Chemical process" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chemical_process">chemical process</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&nbsp;&nbsp;Any method or means of changing one or more&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemical_species"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; chemical species">chemicals</span></a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#compound"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; compound">chemical compounds</span></a>&nbsp;in any way, either naturally or artificially, spontaneously or by the actions of external forces.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&nbsp;&nbsp;In&nbsp;<a title="Chemical engineering" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chemical_engineering">chemical engineering</a>, any method used on an industrial scale (especially in&nbsp;<a title="Manufacturing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manufacturing">manufacturing</a>) to change the composition of one or more chemicals or materials.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="chemical_reaction" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Chemical reaction" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chemical_reaction">chemical reaction</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The change of one or more&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemical_substance"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; chemical substance">substances</span></a>&nbsp;into one or more different substances.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="chemical_species" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Chemical species" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chemical_species">chemical species</a></dfn></dt>
</dl>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><span class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also simply called a&nbsp;<strong>chemical</strong>.</span></p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dd class="glossary">A&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemical_substance"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; chemical substance">chemical substance</span></a>&nbsp;or ensemble of substances composed of chemically identical&nbsp;<a title="Molecular entity" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Molecular_entity">molecular entities</a>&nbsp;which can explore the same set of molecular energy levels on a characteristic or delineated time scale.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="chemical_substance" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Chemical substance" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chemical_substance">chemical substance</a></dfn></dt>
</dl>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><span class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also&nbsp;<strong>pure substance</strong>&nbsp;or simply&nbsp;<strong>substance</strong>.</span></p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dd class="glossary">A form of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#matter"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; matter">matter</span></a>&nbsp;that has constant&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemical_composition"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; chemical composition">chemical composition</span></a>&nbsp;and characteristic&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#physical_property"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; physical property">properties</span></a>&nbsp;and which cannot be separated into simpler components by purely physical methods (i.e. without breaking&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#bond"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; bond">chemical bonds</span></a>). It is often called a&nbsp;<em>pure substance</em>&nbsp;to distinguish it from a&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#mixture"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; mixture">mixture</span></a>.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="chemical_synthesis" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Chemical synthesis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chemical_synthesis">chemical synthesis</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The artificial execution of one or more&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemical_reaction"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; chemical reaction">chemical reactions</span></a>&nbsp;in order to obtain one or more&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#product"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; product">products</span></a>. In modern laboratory contexts, specific chemical syntheses are both reliable and reproducible.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="chemistry" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Chemistry" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chemistry">chemistry</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The scientific discipline that studies&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemical_substance"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; chemical substance">chemical substances</span></a>,&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#compound"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; compound">compounds</span></a>, and&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#molecule"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; molecule">molecules</span></a>&nbsp;composed of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#atom"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; atom">atoms</span></a>&nbsp;of various&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#element"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; element">chemical elements</span></a>, as well as their&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemical_composition"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; chemical composition">compositions</span></a>, structures, properties, behaviors, and the changes they undergo during&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemical_reaction"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; chemical reaction">reactions</span></a>&nbsp;with other substances.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="chirality" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Chirality" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chirality">chirality</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="chromatography" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Chromatography" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chromatography">chromatography</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="cis&ndash;trans_isomerism" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Cis&ndash;trans isomerism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cis%E2%80%93trans_isomerism">cis&ndash;trans isomerism</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="closed_system" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Closed system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Closed_system">closed system</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="cluster" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Cluster chemistry" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cluster_chemistry">cluster</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="cohesion" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Cohesion (chemistry)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cohesion_(chemistry)">cohesion</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The tendency of similar particles or surfaces to cling to one another as a result of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#intermolecular_force"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; intermolecular force">intermolecular forces</span></a>. Contrast&nbsp;<em><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#adhesion"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; adhesion">adhesion</span></a></em>.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="colligative_property" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Colligative property" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colligative_property">colligative property</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Any property of a&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solution"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; solution">solution</span></a>&nbsp;that depends upon the ratio of the number of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solute"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; solute">solute</span></a>&nbsp;particles to the number of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solvent"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; solvent">solvent</span></a>&nbsp;particles in the solution, and not on the nature of the&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemical_species"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; chemical species">chemical species</span></a>&nbsp;present.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="colloid" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Colloid" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colloid">colloid</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#mixture"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; mixture">mixture</span></a>&nbsp;of evenly&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#dispersion"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; dispersion">dispersed</span></a>&nbsp;substances, such as many&nbsp;<a title="Milk" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Milk">milks</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="combustion" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Combustion" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Combustion">combustion</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#exothermic_process"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; exothermic process">exothermic</span></a>&nbsp;reaction between an&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#oxidant"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; oxidant">oxidant</span></a>&nbsp;and a fuel that produces large amounts of heat and often light.</dd>
</dl>
<div class="thumb tright">&nbsp;</div>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="commission_on_isotopic_abundances_and_atomic_weights_(ciaaw)" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Commission on Isotopic Abundances and Atomic Weights" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commission_on_Isotopic_Abundances_and_Atomic_Weights">Commission on Isotopic Abundances and Atomic Weights</a>&nbsp;(CIAAW)</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="compression" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Compression (physics)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Compression_(physics)">compression</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An area in a longitudinal wave where the particles are closer and pushed in.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="compound" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Chemical compound" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chemical_compound">compound</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemical_substance"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; chemical substance">substance</span></a>&nbsp;that is made up of two or more&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#bond"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; bond">chemically bonded</span></a>&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#element"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; element">elements</span></a>.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="concentration" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Concentration" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Concentration">concentration</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The abundance of a constituent of a&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#mixture"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; mixture">mixture</span></a>&nbsp;divided by the total&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#volume"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; volume">volume</span></a>&nbsp;of the mixture. Several different definitions of concentration are widely used in chemistry, including&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#mass_concentration"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; mass concentration">mass concentration</span></a>,&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#volume_concentration"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; volume concentration">volume concentration</span></a>, and&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#molar_concentration"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; molar concentration">molar concentration</span></a>.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="condensation" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Condensation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Condensation">condensation</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#phase_transition"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; phase transition">phase transition</span></a>&nbsp;of a substance from a&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#gas"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; gas">gas</span></a>&nbsp;to a&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#liquid"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; liquid">liquid</span></a>.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="condosity" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Condosity" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Condosity">condosity</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A comparative measurement of the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Electrical conductivity" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electrical_conductivity">electrical conductivity</a>&nbsp;of a&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solution"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; solution">solution</span></a>&nbsp;defined as the&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#molar_concentration"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; molar concentration">molar concentration</span></a>&nbsp;of a&nbsp;<a title="Sodium chloride" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sodium_chloride">sodium chloride</a>&nbsp;(NaCl) solution that has the same specific electrical conductance as the solution under test. It is typically expressed in units of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#mole"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; mole">moles</span></a>&nbsp;per&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#litre"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; litre">litre</span></a>&nbsp;(or per some other unit of volume).</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="conductor" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Electrical conductor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electrical_conductor">conductor</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Any object or material that allows the flow of an&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electric_current"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; electric current">electric current</span></a>&nbsp;in one or more directions. Contrast&nbsp;<em><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#insulator"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; insulator">insulator</span></a></em>.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="conformation" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Conformation (chemistry)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conformation_(chemistry)">conformation</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The spatial arrangement of atoms affording distinction between&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#stereoisomer"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; stereoisomer">stereoisomers</span></a>&nbsp;which can be interconverted by rotations about formally&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#single_bond"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; single bond">single bonds</span></a>.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="conjugate_acid" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Conjugate acid" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conjugate_acid">conjugate acid</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="conjugate_base" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Conjugate base" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conjugate_base">conjugate base</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="conjugated_system" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Conjugated system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conjugated_system">conjugated system</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="cooling_curve" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Cooling curve" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cooling_curve">cooling curve</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="coordinate_chemistry" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary">coordinate chemistry</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="coordinate_covalent_bond" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Coordinate covalent bond" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coordinate_covalent_bond">coordinate covalent bond</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="coordination_complex" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Coordination complex" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coordination_complex">coordination complex</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="corrosion" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Corrosion" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Corrosion">corrosion</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An irreversible interfacial&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemical_reaction"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; chemical reaction">chemical reaction</span></a>&nbsp;of a material with its environment which results in consumption of the material or&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#dissolution"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; dissolution">dissolution</span></a>&nbsp;into the material of an external component of the environment.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="coulomb" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Coulomb" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coulomb">coulomb</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#sI"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; SI">SI</span></a>&nbsp;unit of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electric_charge"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; electric charge">electric charge</span></a>&nbsp;(symbol:&nbsp;<em>C</em>), defined as the charge transported by a constant&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electric_current"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; electric current">current</span></a>&nbsp;of one&nbsp;<a title="Ampere" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ampere">ampere</a>&nbsp;in one&nbsp;<a title="Second" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second">second</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="covalent_bond" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Covalent bond" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Covalent_bond">covalent bond</a></dfn></dt>
</dl>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><span class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also&nbsp;<strong>molecular bond</strong>.</span></p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dd class="glossary">A&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#bond"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; bond">bond</span></a>&nbsp;that involves the sharing of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electron_pair"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; electron pair">electron pairs</span></a>&nbsp;between&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#atom"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; atom">atoms</span></a>. The stable balance of attractive and repulsive forces that occurs between atoms when they share electrons is known as&nbsp;<em>covalent bonding</em>.</dd>
</dl>
<div class="thumb tright">&nbsp;</div>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="critical_point" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Critical point (thermodynamics)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Critical_point_(thermodynamics)">critical point</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The end point of a&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#phase"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; phase">phase</span></a>&nbsp;equilibrium curve or&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#pressure"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; pressure">pressure</span></a>-<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#temperature"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; temperature">temperature</span></a>&nbsp;curve at which conditions are such that phase boundaries vanish and a substance's different phases, such as&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#liquid"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; liquid">liquid</span></a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#vapor"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; vapor">vapor</span></a>, can coexist. The critical point is defined by the intersection of a critical temperature,&nbsp;<em>T<sub>c</sub></em>, and a critical pressure,&nbsp;<em>p<sub>c</sub></em>; above this temperature and pressure, all distinction between phases disappears and the substance becomes a&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#supercritical_fluid"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; supercritical fluid">supercritical fluid</span></a>.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="crystal" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Crystal" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crystal">crystal</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solid"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; solid">solid</span></a>&nbsp;whose constituent particles (such as atoms, ions, or molecules) are arranged in an orderly&nbsp;<a title="Periodic function" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Periodic_function">periodic</a>&nbsp;microscopic structure, forming a&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#lattice"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; lattice">lattice</span></a>&nbsp;that extends in all directions. Such materials are often described as&nbsp;<em>crystalline</em>.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="crystallography" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Crystallography" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crystallography">crystallography</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The branch of chemistry concerned with determining the arrangement of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#atom"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; atom">atoms</span></a>&nbsp;within&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#crystal"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; crystal">crystalline</span></a>&nbsp;solids.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="cuvette" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Cuvette" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cuvette">cuvette</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A type of glassware used in&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#spectroscopy"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; spectroscopy">spectroscopic</span></a>&nbsp;experiments. It is usually made of plastic, glass, or quartz and should be as clean and clear as possible.</dd>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
</dl>
<h2><span id="D" class="mw-headline">D</span></h2>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="d-block" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="D-block" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/D-block">d-block</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="dalton's_law_of_partial_pressures" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Dalton's law" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dalton%27s_law">Dalton's law of partial pressures</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="deionization" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="DI water" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DI_water">deionization</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The removal of ions, and in water's case, mineral ions such as sodium, iron, and calcium.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="deliquescence" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Deliquescence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deliquescence">deliquescence</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A substance's affinity for&nbsp;<a title="Water" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Water">water</a>, often characterized as its tendency to absorb moisture from the atmosphere to form&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#aqueous_solution"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; aqueous solution">aqueous solutions</span></a>. Most strongly deliquescent substances are&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#salt"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; salt">salts</span></a>, such as&nbsp;<a title="Calcium chloride" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Calcium_chloride">calcium chloride</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Potassium carbonate" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Potassium_carbonate">potassium carbonate</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="delocalized_electron" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Delocalized electron" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Delocalized_electron">delocalized electron</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Any&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electron"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; electron">electron</span></a>&nbsp;in a molecule, ion, or solid&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#metal"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; metal">metal</span></a>&nbsp;that is not associated with an individual atom or&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#covalent_bond"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; covalent bond">covalent bond</span></a>. The term may refer to electrons involved in&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#resonance"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; resonance">resonance</span></a>&nbsp;in&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#conjugated_system"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; conjugated system">conjugated systems</span></a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#aromaticity"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; aromaticity">aromatic</span></a>&nbsp;compounds; to&nbsp;<a title="Free electron model" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Free_electron_model">free electrons</a>&nbsp;which facilitate&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Electrical conductivity" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electrical_conductivity">electrical conductivity</a>; or to electrons within delocalized&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#molecular_orbital"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; molecular orbital">molecular orbitals</span></a>&nbsp;encompassing several adjacent atoms.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="density" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Density" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Density">density</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#intensive_property"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; intensive property">intensive property</span></a>&nbsp;of a substance defined as&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#mass"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; mass">mass</span></a>&nbsp;per unit&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#volume"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; volume">volume</span></a>&nbsp;and expressed by the equation&nbsp;<em>d = m/V</em>.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="denticity" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Denticity" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Denticity">denticity</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The number of donor groups in a single&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#ligand"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; ligand">ligand</span></a>&nbsp;that bind to a central atom in a&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#coordination_complex"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; coordination complex">coordination complex</span></a>.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="dependent_variable" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Dependent and independent variables" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dependent_and_independent_variables">dependent variable</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="deposition" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Deposition (chemistry)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deposition_(chemistry)">deposition</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The settling of particles within a solution or mixture.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="dewar_flask" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Dewar flask" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dewar_flask">Dewar flask</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">See&nbsp;<em><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#vacuum_flask"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; vacuum flask">vacuum flask</span></a></em>.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="diatomic" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Diatomic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diatomic">diatomic</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Composed of two atoms, of the same or different elements. Contrast&nbsp;<em><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#monatomic"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; monatomic">monatomic</span></a></em>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<em><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#polyatomic"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; polyatomic">polyatomic</span></a></em>.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="diatomic_molecule" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Diatomic molecule" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diatomic_molecule">diatomic molecule</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Any&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#molecule"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; molecule">molecule</span></a>&nbsp;composed of only two&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#atom"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; atom">atoms</span></a>, of the same or different&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#element"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; element">elements</span></a>.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="diffusion" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Diffusion" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diffusion">diffusion</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The net movement of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#atom"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; atom">atoms</span></a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#molecule"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; molecule">molecules</span></a>&nbsp;from a region of higher concentration to a region of lower concentration. Diffusion is driven by a&nbsp;<a title="Gradient" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gradient">gradient</a>&nbsp;in chemical potential of the diffusing species and depends on the&nbsp;<a title="Random walk" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Random_walk">random walk</a>&nbsp;of particles; hence it results in mixing or mass transport without required directed bulk motion.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="dimer" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Dimer (chemistry)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dimer_(chemistry)">dimer</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#oligomer"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; oligomer">oligomer</span></a>&nbsp;consisting of two&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#monomer"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; monomer">monomers</span></a>&nbsp;joined by chemical bonds that may variably be strong or weak,&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#covalent_bond"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; covalent bond">covalent</span></a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#intermolecular_force"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; intermolecular force">intermolecular</span></a>. A&nbsp;<em>homodimer</em>&nbsp;consists of two identical molecules; a&nbsp;<em>heterodimer</em>&nbsp;consists of two different molecules.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="dipolar_bond" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Dipolar bond" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dipolar_bond">dipolar bond</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="dipole" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Dipole" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dipole">dipole</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The electric or magnetic separation of charge.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="dipole_moment" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Bond dipole moment" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bond_dipole_moment">dipole moment</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The polarity of a polar covalent bond.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="dispersion" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Dispersion (chemistry)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dispersion_(chemistry)">dispersion</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A system in which particles of one material are distributed within a continuous&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#phase"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; phase">phase</span></a>&nbsp;of another material; the two phases may be in the same or different&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#state_of_matter"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; state of matter">states of matter</span></a>. Dispersions of particles sufficiently large for&nbsp;<a title="Sedimentation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sedimentation">sedimentation</a>&nbsp;are called&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#suspension"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; suspension">suspensions</span></a>, while those of smaller particles are called&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#colloid"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; colloid">colloids</span></a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solution"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; solution">solutions</span></a>.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="dissociation" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Dissociation (chemistry)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dissociation_(chemistry)">dissociation</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="dissolution" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Solvation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solvation">dissolution</a></dfn></dt>
</dl>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><span class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also&nbsp;<strong>solvation</strong>.</span></p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dd class="glossary">The interaction of a&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solvent"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; solvent">solvent</span></a>&nbsp;with the molecules or ions of a&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solute"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; solute">solute</span></a>, involving bond formation,&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#hydrogen_bond"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; hydrogen bond">hydrogen bonding</span></a>, and&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#van_der_Waals_force"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; van der Waals force">van der Waals forces</span></a>.</dd>
</dl>
<div class="thumb tright">&nbsp;</div>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="distillation" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Distillation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Distillation">distillation</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The process of separating the component substances of a&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#liquid"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; liquid">liquid</span></a>&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#mixture"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; mixture">mixture</span></a>&nbsp;by exploiting differences in the relative&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#volatility"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; volatility">volatility</span></a>&nbsp;of the mixture's components through selective&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#boiling"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; boiling">boiling</span></a>&nbsp;and subsequent&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#condensation"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; condensation">condensation</span></a>. The apparatus used to distill a substance is called a&nbsp;<em>still</em>, and the re-condensed substance yielded by the process is called the&nbsp;<em>distillate</em>.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="double_bond" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Double bond" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Double_bond">double bond</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#bond"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; bond">bond</span></a>&nbsp;involving the&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#covalent_bond"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; covalent bond">covalent</span></a>&nbsp;sharing of two&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electron_pair"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; electron pair">pairs of electrons</span></a>.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="double-replacement_reaction" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Salt metathesis reaction" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Salt_metathesis_reaction">double-replacement reaction</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="ductility" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Ductility" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ductility">ductility</a></dfn></dt>
</dl>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><span class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also&nbsp;<strong>malleability</strong>.</span></p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dd class="glossary">A measure of a material's ability to undergo significant plastic deformation before rupturing, typically expressed as percent elongation or percent area reduction from a tensile test and popularly characterized by the material's ability to be stretched into a wire.</dd>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
</dl>
<h2><span id="E" class="mw-headline">E</span></h2>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="earth_metal" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary">earth metal</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">See&nbsp;<em><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#alkaline_earth_metal"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; alkaline earth metal">alkaline earth metal</span></a></em>.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="electric_charge" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Electric charge" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electric_charge">electric charge</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A measured property (<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#coulomb"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; coulomb">coulombs</span></a>) that determines&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Electromagnetic interaction" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electromagnetic_interaction">electromagnetic interaction</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="electrolyte" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Electrolyte" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electrolyte">electrolyte</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solution"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; solution">solution</span></a>&nbsp;that conducts a certain amount of electric current and can be split categorically into weak and strong electrolytes.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="electrochemical_cell" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Electrochemical cell" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electrochemical_cell">electrochemical cell</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Using a chemical reaction's current,&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electromotive_force"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; electromotive force">electromotive force</span></a>&nbsp;is made.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="electromagnetic_radiation" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Electromagnetic radiation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electromagnetic_radiation">electromagnetic radiation</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A type of wave that can go through vacuums as well as material and is classified as a self-propagating wave.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="electromagnetic_spectrum" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Electromagnetic spectrum" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electromagnetic_spectrum">electromagnetic spectrum</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="electromagnetism" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Electromagnetism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electromagnetism">electromagnetism</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Fields with an electric charge and electrical properties that change the way that particles move and interact.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="electromotive_force_(emf)" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Electromotive force" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electromotive_force">electromotive force</a>&nbsp;(emf)</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="electron" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Electron" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electron">electron</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A type of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#subatomic_particle"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; subatomic particle">subatomic particle</span></a>&nbsp;with a net charge that is negative.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="electron_configuration" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Electron configuration" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electron_configuration">electron configuration</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The distribution of the&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electron"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; electron">electrons</span></a>&nbsp;of an&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#atom"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; atom">atom</span></a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#molecule"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; molecule">molecule</span></a>&nbsp;within&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#atomic_orbital"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; atomic orbital">atomic</span></a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#molecular_orbital"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; molecular orbital">molecular orbitals</span></a>. An extensive system of notation is used to concisely and uniquely display information about the electron configuration of each atomic species. Knowledge of the specific arrangements of electrons in different atoms is useful for understanding&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#bond"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; bond">chemical bonds</span></a>&nbsp;and the organization of the&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#periodic_table"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; periodic table">periodic table of the elements</span></a>.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="electron_deficiency" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Electron deficiency" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electron_deficiency">electron deficiency</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="electron_pair" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Electron pair" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electron_pair">electron pair</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Two&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electron"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; electron">electrons</span></a>&nbsp;which occupy the same&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#molecular_orbital"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; molecular orbital">molecular orbital</span></a>&nbsp;but have opposite&nbsp;<a title="Spin (physics)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spin_(physics)">spins</a>. Electron pairs form&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#bond"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; bond">chemical bonds</span></a>&nbsp;or occur as&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#lone_pair"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; lone pair">lone pairs</span></a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#valence_electron"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; valence electron">valence electrons</span></a>; it is also possible for electrons to occur individually as&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#unpaired_electron"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; unpaired electron">unpaired electrons</span></a>.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="electron_shell" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Electron shell" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electron_shell">electron shell</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#atomic_orbital"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; atomic orbital">orbital</span></a>&nbsp;around the&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#nucleus"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; nucleus">nucleus</span></a>&nbsp;of an&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#atom"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; atom">atom</span></a>&nbsp;which contains a fixed number of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electron"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; electron">electrons</span></a>&nbsp;(usually two or eight).</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="electronegativity_(&chi;)" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Electronegativity" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electronegativity">electronegativity</a>&nbsp;(<a title="Chi (letter)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chi_(letter)">&chi;</a>)</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A chemical property that describes the tendency of an&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#atom"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; atom">atom</span></a>&nbsp;to attract a shared&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electron_pair"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; electron pair">pair</span></a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electron"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; electron">electrons</span></a>&nbsp;(or&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electron_density"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect; electron density">electron density</span></a>) towards itself.
